(A.) [See also another ex. in art. <foreign lang="ar">رحب</foreign>, conj. 6.]          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  And hence [also], the <foreign lang="ar">مَصَادِر</foreign> [pl. of <foreign lang="ar">مَصْدَر</foreign>] of verbs: (S, TA:) <foreign lang="ar">مَصْدَرٌ</foreign> signifies <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  The <hi rend="ital">root</hi> of a word, <hi rend="ital">from which proceed the derivatives of verbs:</hi> (Lth, TA:) [in this sense it is a conventional term of grammar and lexicology, not belonging to the classical language; but on account of the importance of understanding its true application in lexicology, it is necessary to give here a full explanation of it: it is, agreeably with its etymology, the <hi rend="ital">source</hi> (lit. place) <hi rend="ital">of derivation,</hi> accord. to the grammarians of ElBasrah; and is what I term <hi rend="ital">an infinitive noun:</hi> it is defined as] <hi rend="ital">a noun signifying, by its original application, an accident as subsisting in,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">proceeding from, an agent</hi> (as <foreign lang="ar">الفَرَحُ</foreign> [“ the being joyful ”], <foreign lang="ar">الضَّرْبُ</foreign> [“ the act of beating ”], and <foreign lang="ar">القُعُودُ</foreign> [“ the act of sitting ”]), or <hi rend="ital">affecting an object of action,</hi> (as <foreign lang="ar">الجُنُونُ</foreign> [“ the being possessed by a jinnee ”]), <hi rend="ital">conformable to its verb, so as to comprise all the letters in that verb, either literally</hi> (as in the instances above) <hi rend="ital">or virtually</hi> (as in <foreign lang="ar">القِتَالُ</foreign> [“ the act of fighting ”], which wants the <foreign lang="ar">ا</foreign> that is before the <foreign lang="ar">ت</foreign> in the verb, yet wants it as to the letter only, and not virtually, wherefore it is sometimes pronounced as if with the said letter, as in <foreign lang="ar">قَاتَلَ قِيتَالًا</foreign>, but the <foreign lang="ar">ا</foreign> is changed into <foreign lang="ar">ى</foreign> on account of the kesr of the letter before it), or <hi rend="ital">substituting another letter for any of those letters that it wants</hi> (as in <foreign lang="ar">العِدَةُ</foreign> [“ the act of promising ”], which wants the <foreign lang="ar">و</foreign> that is in its verb as to the letter and virtually, but has <foreign lang="ar">ة</foreign> substituted for it [by way of compensation]): (from a comparison of definitions &amp;c. in the Expos. of the “ Kitab Hodood en-Nahw ” by the author of the work thus entitled, arts. <foreign lang="ar">مصدر</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">اسم مصدر</foreign>; the Expos. of the “ Shudhoor edh-Dhahab ” by the author of the work thus entitled, section on the nouns that govern as verbs; I' Ak; &amp;c.:) but the grammarians of El-Koofeh hold that the verb is the root, and that the <foreign lang="ar">مصدر</foreign> is derived from it: (I' Ak p. 148:) some <foreign lang="ar">مصادر</foreign>, moreover, are derived from real (as opposed to ideal) substantives, as <foreign lang="ar">التَّحَجُّرُ</foreign> [“ the becoming stone ”] from <foreign lang="ar">الحَجَرُ</foreign> [“ stone ”]. (Kull p. 327.) The <foreign lang="ar">مصدر</foreign> has the same government as its own verb: it is often, and may be at pleasure, used as an ideal subst. or abstract noun: and it is often employed in the place of an act. or a pass. part. n.: (Kull, &amp;c.:) [when thus used as an epithet, it is employed alike as sing. and pl. and masc. and fem.:] accord. to Zj, every <foreign lang="ar">مصدر</foreign> used as an epithet is for <foreign lang="ar">ذُو</foreign> [or <foreign lang="ar">ذَات</foreign> &amp;c.] followed by the <foreign lang="ar">مصدر</foreign>, and therefore it has no dual nor pl. [nor fem.] form. (TA voce <foreign lang="ar">حَرَضٌ</foreign>.) [It has also other uses, which are expl. in the grammars. Used as a <foreign lang="ar">مَصْدَر</foreign>, it is sometimes made fem.; as it is also when used in the sense of a noun that is properly fem.: see <foreign lang="ar">صَرْفٌ</foreign>, third sentence.]          <sense type="b" n="4">-b4-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">اِسْمُ مَصْدَرٍ</foreign>, called by some <foreign lang="ar">اِسْمٌ لِلْمَصْدَرِ</foreign>, is a term applied to [<assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">A quasi-infinitive noun;</hi> i. e.] <hi rend="ital">a noun which is not a</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">مصدر</foreign>, <hi rend="ital">but which is occasionally used in the place of a</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">مصدر</foreign>; like as a <foreign lang="ar">مصدر</foreign> is used in the place of an act. part. n., and in that of a pass. part. n.: such as <foreign lang="ar">الوُضُوْءُ</foreign> for <foreign lang="ar">التَّوَضُّؤُ</foreign> [“ the performing of the ablution preparatory to prayer ”], and <foreign lang="ar">الغُسْلُ</foreign> for <foreign lang="ar">الاِغْتِسَالُ</foreign> [“ the washing of oneself ”]; each of which wants somewhat that is in its verb without substituting anything for that which is wanting. (Expos. of the “ Kitáb el- Hodood, ” cited above.) This kind of noun the grammarians of El-Koofeh and Baghdád allow to govern as a <foreign lang="ar">مصدر</foreign>; but the grammarians of ElBasrah hold that the noun governed in the accus. case in each of the exs. adduced by the former as confirmatory of their opinion is so governed by a verb understood. (Expos. of the “ Shudhoor, ” ubi suprà.) It is also applied to <hi rend="ital">A proper name signifying an accident</hi> [or <hi rend="ital">attribute</hi>]; as <foreign lang="ar">فَجَارِ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">حَمَادِ</foreign>, proper names, by original application, for <foreign lang="ar">الفَجْرَةُ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">المَحْمَدَةُ</foreign> [“ vice ” and “ praise ”] and the like: and this kind does not govern as a <foreign lang="ar">مصدر</foreign>. (Expos. of the “ Kitáb Hodood enNahw, ” ubi suprà; and Expos. of the “ Shudhoor, ” ubi suprà.) It is also applied to [what is more properly termed <foreign lang="ar">اِسْمٌ لِلْمَعْنَى الحَاصِلِ بِالمَصْدَرِ</foreign>, by some termed simply <foreign lang="ar">حَاصِلٌ بِالمَصْدَرِ</foreign>, i. e. <hi rend="ital">An ideal substantive,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">abstract noun;</hi>] <hi rend="ital">a noun applied to signify an accident</hi> [or <hi rend="ital">attribute</hi>] <hi rend="ital">considered abstractedly</hi> [such as <foreign lang="ar">صَدَرٌ</foreign> signifying “ return; ” and this kind is commonly termed in the lexicons simply an <foreign lang="ar">اِسْم</foreign> as distinguished from a <foreign lang="ar">مصدر</foreign>].                   <foreign lang="ar">مصدر</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">commencing with an augmentative</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">م</foreign>], if not of the measure <foreign lang="ar">مُفَاعَلَةٌ</foreign>: but such is really a <foreign lang="ar">مَصْدَر</foreign>.
